## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. In such systems, the restoring force is typically a nonlinear function of displacement (e.g., cubic terms like Duffing oscillator), and damping may depend nonlinearly on velocity. The acceleration equation is essentially Newton's second law applied to the oscillator.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring force with linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring force with linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping depending on position)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 (odd-power nonlinear damping)
- Driven nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (Duffing with periodic forcing)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent effective stiffness)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated restoring force)
- Mixed nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Combined position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**3 (cross-coupling between position and velocity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells, preserving oscillator symmetry under x → -x
- Even-power position terms (x**2) → asymmetric potential, indicating broken symmetry in the restoring force
- Velocity-dependent terms linear in v → linear energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Product terms like x**2 * v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type nonlinearity
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force
- Cubic position term with opposite sign to linear term → double-well (Duffing) potential with bistability
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence suggests forcing or parametric excitation
- Odd-power velocity terms (v**3) → nonlinear damping that preserves time-reversal symmetry breaking consistently

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-2.5126990598325*x**3 - 2.5126990598325*x*(0.0921849151045819*t + 1) - 0.774919680656294*sin(v)`

Expanding: `-2.5126990598325*x**3 - 2.5126990598325*0.0921849151045819*t*x - 2.5126990598325*x - 0.774919680656294*sin(v)`

So GT = `A*x + B*x**3 + C*t*x + D*sin(v)` where A, B, C are specific constants and D is the coefficient of sin(v).

The key basis functions are: **x, x³, t·x, sin(v)**

Let me systematically check each candidate for whether it can produce exactly these basis functions.

**Candidate 1:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*v) + c4*v + c5*x*cos(c6*t) + c7*v*x*cos(c8*t)`
- Has x, x³, sin(c3*v) (set c3=1), set c4=0 to kill v term. But has x*cos(c6*t) and v*x*cos(c8*t) instead of t*x. cos(c6*t) is not equivalent to t. Set c5=0, c7=0, but then no t*x term. **Cannot produce t*x.**
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** Simplify: `c0*v/(c1*v²+1) + c2*x + c3*x³ + c4*v + c5*x*cos(c6*t) + c7*v*x*cos(c8*t)`
- The term c0*v/(c1*v²+1) cannot be reduced to sin(v) or t*x. Missing t*x term. Has cos(t) terms instead.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*x*cos(c4*t) + c5*v*x*cos(c6*t) + c7*v**3`
- Has v instead of sin(v), has cos(t) terms instead of t*x. Cannot match.
Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*(c4*x + c5*v)) + c6*t*x + v`
- Has x, x³, t*x, v (coefficient 1, fixed). Has sin(c3*(c4*x + c5*v)). If we set c4=0, this becomes sin(c3*c5*v) which can match sin(v). But then we have a fixed `v` term with coefficient 1. GT has no standalone v term. The GT has -0.775*sin(v), not a linear v term. We can't eliminate the `v` term (coefficient is 1, not adjustable).
Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** `(c0*v + c1 + (c2*t + c3)*(c4*x + c5*x**3 + c6*v + c7*v**3))/(c2*t + c3)`
Expand: `c0*v/(c2*t+c3) + c1/(c2*t+c3) + c4*x + c5*x**3 + c6*v + c7*v**3`
- Has terms c0*v/(c2*t+c3) and c1/(c2*t+c3) which are rational in t. These can't be zeroed unless c0=c1=0. Then we get c4*x + c5*x³ + c6*v + c7*v³. Missing t*x and sin(v). v³ ≠ sin(v).
Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 6:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*x*cos(c4*t) + c5*v*x*cos(c6*t) + c7*log(c8*exp(c9*v) + 1)`
- log(c8*exp(c9*v)+1) is a softplus, not sin(v). Has cos(t) terms, not t*x.
Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*v) + c4*x**3 + c5*t**c6*x`
- Has x, v, sin(c3*v), x³, t^c6 * x. Set c3=1 for sin(v). Set c6=1 for t*x. Then: c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(v) + c4*x³ + c5*t*x. GT has no standalone v term. Set c1=0. Then: c0*x + c2*sin(v) + c4*x³ + c5*t*x. This matches the GT structure!
Candidate 7 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*x**3 + c3*v**3 + c4*t**c5*x`
- Has v and v³ but no sin(v). v and v³ cannot combine to equal sin(v).
Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

- Has x, x³, sin(c3*v) (set c3=1), v (set c4=0), t*x. Perfect match!
Candidate 9 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 10:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*x + c3*t*x + c4*v + c5*v**3`
- (c0+c2)*x + c1*x³ + c3*t*x + c4*v + c5*v³. Has v and v³ but no sin(v). Cannot match.
Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

- v and v³ cannot equal sin(v).
